    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           1,66
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,05
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 24.3 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.66 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.05 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    smsp__issue_active.avg.per_cycle_active                                                                          0,04
    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                    17,82
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                        17,41
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 14.2 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 35.3% of the total average of 40.3 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 17.4 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 43.3% of the total average of 40.3   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 17.8 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 17.4 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    smsp__warps_active.avg.peak_sustained                                             warp                              8
    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           1,78
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,04
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 29.9 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.78 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.04 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    smsp__issue_active.avg.per_cycle_active                                                                          0,03
    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                    21,32
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                        20,92
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 20.4 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 38.5% of the total average of 53.1 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 20.4 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 38.4% of the total average of 53.1   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 21.3 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 20.9 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           1,55
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,05
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 24.3 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.55 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.05 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                    17,23
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                        16,91
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 14.3 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 37.9% of the total average of 37.7 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 17.0 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 45.2% of the total average of 37.7   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 17.2 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 16.9 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    Active Warps Per Scheduler                                                        warp                           1,54
    Eligible Warps Per Scheduler                                                      warp                           0,04
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 31.4 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.54 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.04 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    Avg. Active Threads Per Warp                                                                                    20,48
    Avg. Not Predicated Off Threads Per Warp                                                                        20,14
    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 20.1 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 41.6% of the total average of 48.4 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 20.0 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 41.3% of the total average of 48.4   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 20.5 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 20.1 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 25.3 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.47 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.04 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 14.2 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 38.1% of the total average of 37.2 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 16.5 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 44.4% of the total average of 37.2   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 16.1 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 16.0 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 29.7 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.60 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.04 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 19.7 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 41.4% of the total average of 47.6 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 20.1 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 42.2% of the total average of 47.6   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 18.5 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 18.2 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 25.7 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.47 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.04 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    ---------------------------------------------------------------------- --------------- ------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 14.4 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 38.1% of the total average of 37.7 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 17.2 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 45.5% of the total average of 37.7   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 15.0 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 14.9 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 32.4 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.49 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.04 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 20.2 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 41.8% of the total average of 48.4 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 20.4 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 42.2% of the total average of 48.4   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 18.8 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 18.6 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 25.1 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.68 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.05 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 20.8 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 49.5% of the total average of 42.1 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 19.8 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 47.0% of the total average of 42.1   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 17.5 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 17.5 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().

    WRN   Every scheduler is capable of issuing one instruction per cycle, but for this kernel each scheduler only      
          issues an instruction every 30.4 cycles. This might leave hardware resources underutilized and may lead to    
          less optimal performance. Out of the maximum of 8 warps per scheduler, this kernel allocates an average of    
          1.84 active warps per scheduler, but only an average of 0.04 warps were eligible per cycle. Eligible warps    
          are the subset of active warps that are ready to issue their next instruction. Every cycle with no eligible   
          warp results in no instruction being issued and the issue slot remains unused. To increase the number of      
          eligible warps either increase the number of active warps or reduce the time the active warps are stalled.

    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 22.8 cycles being stalled waiting for an immediate constant cache  
          (IMC) miss. This represents about 40.8% of the total average of 56.0 cycles between issuing two               
          instructions. A read from constant memory costs one memory read from global memory only on a cache miss;      
          otherwise, it just costs one read from the constant cache. Immediate constants are encoded into the SASS      
          instruction as 'c[bank][offset]'. All threads access the same value.                                          
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   On average each warp of this kernel spends 20.9 cycles being stalled waiting for a scoreboard dependency on a 
          L1TEX (local, global, surface, texture) operation. This represents about 37.4% of the total average of 56.0   
          cycles between issuing two instructions. To reduce the number of cycles waiting on L1TEX data accesses        
          verify the memory access patterns are optimal for the target architecture, attempt to increase cache hit      
          rates by increasing data locality or by changing the cache configuration, and consider moving frequently      
          used data to shared memory.                                                                                   
    ----- --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    WRN   Instructions are executed in warps, which are groups of 32 threads. Optimal instruction throughput is         
          achieved if all 32 threads of a warp execute the same instruction. The chosen launch configuration, early     
          thread completion, and divergent flow control can significantly lower the number of active threads in a warp  
          per cycle. This kernel achieves an average of 20.5 threads being active per cycle. This is further reduced    
          to 20.5 threads per warp due to predication. The compiler may use predication to avoid an actual branch.      
          Instead, all instructions are scheduled, but a per-thread condition code or predicate controls which threads  
          execute the instructions. Try to avoid different execution paths within a warp when possible. In addition,    
          ensure your kernel makes use of Independent Thread Scheduling, which allows a warp to reconverge after a      
          data-dependent conditional block by explicitly calling __syncwarp().
